## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical kinetics
**Analysis**: This task models the time evolution of a chemical species in a reaction system, where the rate of concentration change depends on current concentration and time. The relationship typically follows mass-action rate laws, autocatalytic feedback, or time-modulated mechanisms like catalyst deactivation.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order rate law: dA_dt = -c0 (constant reaction rate independent of concentration)
- First-order mass action: dA_dt = -c0 * A (rate linearly proportional to reactant amount)
- Second-order mass action: dA_dt = -c0 * A**2 (rate proportional to collision frequency of identical species)
- Autocatalytic feedback: dA_dt = c0 * A * (1 - c1 * A) (self-accelerating reaction with natural limit)
- Concentration-inhibited rate: dA_dt = -c0 * A / (1 + c1 * A) (reaction slows at high concentrations due to crowding)
- Catalyst deactivation model: dA_dt = -c0 * A * exp(c1 * t) (reactant consumption rate decreases exponentially over time)
- Induction-phase kinetics: dA_dt = -c0 * A * (1 + c1 * t)**c2 (rate modulated by time-dependent activation delay)
- Reversible first-order dynamics: dA_dt = -c0 * A + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (net rate from forward consumption and backward regeneration)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Elementary reaction molecularity → Integer power-law dependence on concentration (A**n)
- Catalyst deactivation or thermal degradation → Multiplicative time-decay factor exp(c*t) scaling the concentration term
- Autocatalytic or chain-branching dynamics → Bilinear concentration form A*(c1 - A) yielding a parabolic rate profile
- Diffusion-controlled reaction limit → Time-modulated pre-factor such as t**c1 multiplying the concentration dependence
- Reversible reaction relaxation → Difference of opposing rate terms (c0 * A - c1 * B) or linear combination approaching zero
- Product inhibition or steric crowding → Rational suppression factor 1/(1 + c1 * A) scaling the baseline consumption rate
- Competing parallel pathways → Additive sum of independent concentration-dependent terms representing distinct mechanisms

### Analysis of Candidates

The Ground Truth (GT) expression is:
`GT = -0.19494483384724354 * A + 0.24819026785686927 * cos(log(A + 1))`
This function consists of two linearly independent basis functions:
1. A linear term in `A`: `k1 * A`
2. A transcendental term: `k2 * cos(log(A + 1))`

To match the GT, a candidate must be able to reduce to the form `c_A * A + c_C * cos(log(A + c))` (or equivalent using `sin` with a phase shift). Candidates containing only polynomials, rational functions, exponentials, or trigonometric functions of linear `A` cannot match the `cos(log(A))` term due to linear independence of basis functions.

**Candidate 16:** `A*(A*c0 + c1) + c2*log(A*c3 + 1) + c4*sin(c5*log(A*c6 + 1) + c7)`
- Set `c0 = 0` to eliminate the quadratic term.
- Set `c2 = 0` to eliminate the standalone logarithm term.
- The expression reduces to `A*c1 + c4*sin(c5*log(A*c6 + 1) + c7)`.
- By setting `c1 = -0.1949...`, `c6 = 1`, `c5 = 1`, `c7 = π/2`, and `c4 = 0.2481...`, it exactly matches `k1*A + k2*cos(log(A+1))`.
- **Verdict: MATCH**

**Candidate 27:** `A*(A*c0 + c1) + c2*sin(c3*log(A*c4 + 1) + c5)`
- Set `c0 = 0` to eliminate the quadratic term.
- Reduces to `A*c1 + c2*sin(c3*log(A*c4 + 1) + c5)`.
- Setting `c1 = -0.1949...`, `c4 = 1`, `c3 = 1`, `c5 = π/2`, `c2 = 0.2481...` yields exact equivalence.
- **Verdict: MATCH**

**Candidate 28:** `A**(1/3)*c0 + A*c1 + c2*sin(c3*log(A*c4 + 1) + c5)`
- Set `c0 = 0` to eliminate the cube-root term.
- Reduces to `A*c1 + c2*sin(c3*log(A*c4 + 1) + c5)`.
- Identical functional form to Candidate 27 after zeroing `c0`. Matches GT exactly with appropriate constant assignments.
- **Verdict: MATCH**

**All Other Candidates (1-15, 17-26, 29-89):**
- Lack the required `sin(log(...))` or `cos(log(...))` structure.
- Contain incompatible basis functions (e.g., `sin(A)`, `exp(A)`, `sqrt(A)`, rational functions, or standalone `log(A)` without trigonometric wrapping).
- Due to the linear independence of polynomials, exponentials, and trigonometric/logarithmic compositions, none can be algebraically manipulated to exactly equal `cos(log(A + 1))` across the continuous domain.
- **Verdict: NO MATCH**

GT: -c0*A + c1*_w*cos(log(A + c2))

I need to determine which candidates can be made equivalent to the GT:

**GT: `-0.19494483384724354*A + 0.24819026785686927*cos(log(A + 1))`**

Note that `c1*_w = 0.19494483384724354 * 1.27313... = 0.24819...`, and `c2 = 1`.

So GT = `-0.195*A + 0.248*cos(log(A + 1))`

The key basis functions are: `A` (linear) and `cos(log(A + 1))` (cosine of logarithm).

Let me analyze each candidate, focusing on whether they can produce exactly these basis functions.

**Key observations:**
- The GT has NO dependence on `t` (unless t-coefficients can be zeroed)
- The GT has NO `A^2`, `A^(1/3)`, `sqrt(A)`, `exp(A)`, `1/A^(1/3)` terms
- The GT has `cos(log(A+1))` which is a very specific transcendental function
- `sin(log(A+c) + c)` can match `cos(log(A+1))` via phase shift
- `log(A+1)` alone cannot match `cos(log(A+1))`
- `sin(A*c)` or `cos(A*c)` cannot match `cos(log(A+1))`

Let me go through candidates systematically:

**Candidates with `t` dependence (1, 2, 54, 55, 60):**
- **Candidate 1**: `A²c0 + Ac1 + (c2*t+c3)/(c4*t+c5) + c6/A^(1/3)` — Set c0=0, c6=0, then `Ac1 + c3/c5`. This is linear+constant, missing `cos(log(A+1))`. **NO MATCH**
- **Candidate 2**: Simplifies to `A²c2 + Ac3 + c4*log(Ac5+1) + (c0*t+c1)/(c6*t+c7)`. Set c0=0 to kill t, get `A²c2+Ac3+c4*log(Ac5+1)+c1/c7`. Missing cos(log). **NO MATCH**
- **Candidate 54**: `A^(1/3)*c0 + A*c3 + (c4+t)/(c1*t+c2)`. Set c4+t terms: need c1≠0, then t/(c1*t+c2) can't be eliminated for all t unless... actually (c4+t)/(c1*t+c2) has t-dependence that can't be zeroed unless coefficient structure allows. If c1=0, get (c4+t)/c2 which still has t. **NO MATCH**
- **Candidate 55**: Simplifies to `Ac2 + c3*log(Ac4+1) + (c0*t+c1)/(c5*t+c6)`. Set c0=0: `Ac2+c3*log(Ac4+1)+c1/c6`. Missing cos(log). **NO MATCH**
- **Candidate 60**: `A²c0+Ac1 + (c4*t+c5)/(c2*t+c3)`. Set c4=0: `A²c0+Ac1+c5/c3`. Set c0=0: linear+const. **NO MATCH**

**Candidates with `sin(c*log(A*c+1)+c)` or `cos(c*log(A*c+1)+c)`:**

- **Candidate 16**: `A(Ac0+c1) + c2*log(Ac3+1) + c4*sin(c5*log(Ac6+1)+c7)`. Set c0=0, c2=0: `Ac1 + c4*sin(c5*log(Ac6+1)+c7)`. With c6=1, c5=1, c7=π/2: `Ac1 + c4*cos(log(A+1))`. **MATCH!**

- **Candidate 27**: `A(Ac0+c1) + c2*sin(c3*log(Ac4+1)+c5)`. Set c0=0: `Ac1 + c2*sin(c3*log(Ac4+1)+c5)`. With c4=1, c3=1, c5=π/2: **MATCH!**

- **Candidate 28**: `A^(1/3)*c0 + Ac1 + c2*sin(c3*log(Ac4+1)+c5)`. Set c0=0, c4=1, c3=1, c5=π/2: `Ac1 + c2*cos(log(A+1))`. **MATCH!**

- **Candidate 35**: `Ac0 + c1 + c2*sin(c3*log(c4*|A|+1)+1)`. With A≥0, |A|=A. Set c4 appropriately, c3=1, but the phase is fixed at 1, not π/2. Since 1 ≠ π/2, and the phase `+1` is a fixed constant (not a free parameter labeled `c`), this cannot match. Wait - looking again, the `+1` at the end is explicit, not a free constant. So phase = 1 radian, not adjustable. **NO MATCH**

Let me verify all remaining candidates quickly for the `cos(log(...))` pattern. None of the other candidates contain `sin(log(...))` or `cos(log(...))` constructions, so they cannot match.

**Candidate 16 verdict: [MATCH]**
**Candidate 27 verdict: [MATCH]**
**Candidate 28 verdict: [MATCH]**
